<tr class="mergedrow">
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Geographic_Names_Information_System" title="Geographic Names Information System">GNIS</a> feature IDs</th>

<tr class="mergedtoprow">
<th scope="row">Website</th>

</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Glendale</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ɛ/ short 'e' in 'bed'">ɛ</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/eɪ/ long 'a' in 'base'">eɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span></span> is a city in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County,_California" title="Los Angeles County, California">Los Angeles County</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>, United States. Its estimated 2014 population was 200,167,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-est2014_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-est2014-8">[8]</a></sup> making it the third largest city in Los Angeles County and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_largest_California_cities_by_population" title="List of largest California cities by population">23rd-largest city in California</a>. It is located about 8 miles (13 km) north of downtown <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.</p>
<p>Glendale lies on the southeastern end of the <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando_Valley" title="San Fernando Valley">San Fernando Valley</a>, bisected by the <a href="/wiki/Verdugo_Mountains" title="Verdugo Mountains">Verdugo Mountains</a>, and is a <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">suburb</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Los_Angeles_Area" title="Greater Los Angeles Area">Greater Los Angeles Area</a>. The city is bordered to the northwest by the <a href="/wiki/Sun_Valley,_Los_Angeles" title="Sun Valley, Los Angeles">Sun Valley</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tujunga,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Tujunga, Los Angeles, California">Tujunga</a> neighborhoods of Los Angeles; to the northeast by <a href="/wiki/La_Ca%C3%B1ada_Flintridge,_California" title="La Cañada Flintridge, California">La Cañada Flintridge</a> and the unincorporated area of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Crescenta,_California" title="La Crescenta, California">La Crescenta</a>; to the west by <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Griffith_Park" title="Griffith Park">Griffith Park</a>; to the east by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eagle_Rock,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Eagle Rock, Los Angeles, California">Eagle Rock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena</a>; to the south by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atwater_Village,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Atwater Village, Los Angeles, California">Atwater Village</a> neighborhood of Los Angeles; and to the southeast by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glassell_Park,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Glassell Park, Los Angeles, California">Glassell Park</a> neighborhood of Los Angeles. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_State_Freeway" title="Golden State Freeway">Golden State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ventura_Freeway" title="Ventura Freeway">Ventura</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glendale_Freeway" title="Glendale Freeway">Glendale</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foothill_Freeway" title="Foothill Freeway">Foothill</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freeway" title="Freeway">freeways</a> run through the city.</p>
<p>Glendale has one of the largest communities of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian-American" title="Armenian-American">Armenian</a> descent in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> In 2013, Glendale was named LA's Neighborhood of the Year by the readers and editors of <a href="/wiki/Curbed" title="Curbed">Curbed.com</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forest_Lawn_Memorial_Park,_Glendale" title="Forest Lawn Memorial Park, Glendale">Forest Lawn Memorial Park Cemetery</a> contains the remains of many noted celebrities and local residents. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Airport_(United_States)" title="Grand Central Airport (United States)">Grand Central Airport</a> was the departure point for the first commercial west-to-east transcontinental flight flown by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lindbergh" title="Charles Lindbergh">Charles Lindbergh</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glendale-1870s.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="356" data-file-width="800" height="98" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Glendale-1870s.jpg/220px-Glendale-1870s.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Glendale-1870s.jpg/330px-Glendale-1870s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Glendale-1870s.jpg/440px-Glendale-1870s.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glendale-1870s.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Glendale area in the 1870s</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The area was long inhabited by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tongva_people" title="Tongva people">Tongva people</a> (or "People of the Earth"), who were later renamed the Gabrieleños by the Spanish missionaries, after the nearby <a href="/wiki/Mission_San_Gabriel_Arc%C3%A1ngel" title="Mission San Gabriel Arcángel">Mission San Gabriel Arcángel</a>.</p>
<p>In 1798, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_Maria_Verdugo" title="Jose Maria Verdugo">José María Verdugo</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Corporal" title="Corporal">corporal</a> in the Spanish army from <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California</a>, received the <a href="/wiki/Rancho_San_Rafael" title="Rancho San Rafael">Rancho San Rafael</a> from Governor <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Borica" title="Diego de Borica">Diego de Borica</a>, formalizing his possession and use of land on which he had been grazing livestock and farming since 1784. Rancho San Rafael was a Spanish concession, of which 25 were made in California. Unlike the later Mexican land grants, the concessions were similar to grazing permits, with the title remaining with the Spanish crown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1860, his grandson <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_Maria_Verdugo#Julio_Verdugo" title="Jose Maria Verdugo">Teodoro Verdugo</a> built the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Verdugo_Adobe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Verdugo Adobe (page does not exist)">Verdugo Adobe</a>, which is the oldest building in Glendale. The property is the location of the Oak of Peace, where early <a href="/wiki/Californio" title="Californio">Californio</a> leaders including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pio_Pico" title="Pio Pico">Pio Pico</a> met in 1847 and decided to surrender to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Colonel" title="Lieutenant Colonel">Lieutenant Colonel</a> <a href="/wiki/John_C._Fr%C3%A9mont" title="John C. Frémont">John C. Frémont</a>.</p>
<p>Verdugo's descendants sold the ranch in various parcels, some of which are included in present-day <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atwater_Village,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Atwater Village, Los Angeles, California">Atwater Village</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eagle_Rock,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Eagle Rock, Los Angeles, California">Eagle Rock</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Highland_Park,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Highland Park, Los Angeles, California">Highland Park</a> neighborhoods of Los Angeles.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glendale-1910.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="800" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Glendale-1910.jpg/220px-Glendale-1910.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Glendale-1910.jpg/330px-Glendale-1910.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Glendale-1910.jpg/440px-Glendale-1910.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glendale-1910.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Glendale, 1910</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1884, residents gathered to form a townsite and chose the name "Glendale" (it was bounded by First Street (now Lexington Drive) on the north, Fifth Street (now Harvard Street) on the south, Central Avenue on the west, and the Childs Tract on the east).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> Residents to the southwest formed "Tropico" in 1887. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_Electric_Railway" title="Pacific Electric Railway">Pacific Electric Railway</a> brought streetcar service in 1904.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Glendale incorporated in 1906, and annexed Tropico 12 years later. An important civic <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/booster" title="wiktionary:booster">booster</a> of the era was <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Coombs_Brand" title="Leslie Coombs Brand">Leslie Coombs Brand</a> (1859–1925), who built an estate in 1904 called El Miradero, featuring an eye-catching mansion, the architecture of which combined characteristics of Spanish, Moorish, and Indian styles, copied from the East Indian Pavilion at the 1893 <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Columbian_Exposition" title="World's Columbian Exposition">World's Columbian Exposition</a> held in Chicago, which he visited. Brand loved to fly, and built a private airstrip in 1919 and hosted "fly-in" parties, providing a direct link to the soon-to-be-built nearby <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Central_Airport_(United_States)" title="Grand Central Airport (United States)">Grand Central Airport</a>. The grounds of El Miradero are now city-owned Brand Park and the mansion is the Brand Library, according to the terms of his will.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> Brand partnered with <a href="/wiki/Henry_E._Huntington" title="Henry E. Huntington">Henry E. Huntington</a> to bring the Pacific Electric Railway, or the "Red Cars", to the area. Today, he is memorialized by one of the city's main thoroughfares, Brand Boulevard.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glendale-Brand-1915.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="613" data-file-width="800" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Glendale-Brand-1915.jpg/220px-Glendale-Brand-1915.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Glendale-Brand-1915.jpg/330px-Glendale-Brand-1915.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Glendale-Brand-1915.jpg/440px-Glendale-Brand-1915.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glendale-Brand-1915.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Looking south on Brand Blvd, 1915</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city's population rose from 13,756 in 1920 to 62,736 in 1930. The Forest Lawn Cemetery opened in 1906 and was renamed <a href="/wiki/Forest_Lawn_Memorial_Park_(Glendale)" title="Forest Lawn Memorial Park (Glendale)">Forest Lawn Memorial-Park</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> in 1917. Pioneering <a href="/wiki/Endocrinology" title="Endocrinology">endocrinologist</a> and entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Henry_Harrower" title="Henry Harrower">Henry R. Harrower</a> opened his clinic in Glendale in 1920, which for many years was the largest business in the city. The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=American_Green_Cross&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="American Green Cross (page does not exist)">American Green Cross</a>, an early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conservation_ethic" title="Conservation ethic">conservation</a> and tree preservation society, was formed in 1926 (it disbanded three years later and the current organization of that name is unrelated). In 1964, Glendale was selected by <a href="/wiki/George_Lincoln_Rockwell" title="George Lincoln Rockwell">George Lincoln Rockwell</a> to be the West Coast headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/American_Nazi_Party" title="American Nazi Party">American Nazi Party</a>. Its offices, on Colorado Street in the downtown section of the city, remained open until the early 1980s.</p>
<p>In 1977 and 1978, 10 murdered women were found in and around Glendale in what became known as the case of the <a href="/wiki/Hillside_Strangler" title="Hillside Strangler">Hillside Strangler</a>. The murders were the work of <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Bianchi" title="Kenneth Bianchi">Kenneth Bianchi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angelo_Buono" title="Angelo Buono">Angelo Buono</a>, the latter of whom resided at 703 East Colorado Street, where most of the murders took place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glendale_panorama.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="717" data-file-width="1598" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Glendale_panorama.jpg/350px-Glendale_panorama.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Glendale_panorama.jpg/525px-Glendale_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Glendale_panorama.jpg/700px-Glendale_panorama.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glendale_panorama.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Glendale from <a href="/wiki/Griffith_Park" title="Griffith Park">Griffith Park</a> in the southwest, with the <a href="/wiki/San_Gabriel_Mountains" title="San Gabriel Mountains">San Gabriel Mountains</a> in the background and the Verdugo Hills on the extreme left</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Glendale is located at the junction of two large valleys, the <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando_Valley" title="San Fernando Valley">San Fernando</a> and the <a href="/wiki/San_Gabriel_Valley" title="San Gabriel Valley">San Gabriel</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a>, the city has a total area of 79.212 km<sup>2</sup> (30.6 sq mi); 30.5 square miles (79 km<sup>2</sup>) of it is land and 0.13 square miles (0.34 km<sup>2</sup>) of it (0.43%) is covered by water. It is bordered to the north by the foothill communities of <a href="/wiki/La_Ca%C3%B1ada_Flintridge,_California" title="La Cañada Flintridge, California">La Cañada Flintridge</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Crescenta,_California" title="La Crescenta, California">La Crescenta</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tujunga" title="Tujunga">Tujunga</a>; to the south by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atwater_Village" title="Atwater Village">Atwater Village</a> community incorporated by the city of Los Angeles; to the east by <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eagle_Rock,_California" title="Eagle Rock, California">Eagle Rock</a> (also incorporated within Los Angeles); and to the west by the city of <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank</a>. Glendale is located 10 miles (16 km) north of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Los_Angeles" title="Downtown Los Angeles">downtown Los Angeles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Texeirap1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Texeirap1-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several known earthquake faults criss-cross the Glendale area and adjacent mountains, as in much of Southern California. Among the more recognized faults are the Sierra Madre and Hollywood faults, situated in the city's northern and southwestern portions, respectively. Additionally, the Verdugo and Raymond faults intersect through the city's central and southeastern areas. The San Gabriel fault, meanwhile, is located northeast of the city. Roughly 75 miles (121 km) northeast of Glendale is a major portion of the <a href="/wiki/San_Andreas_Fault" title="San Andreas Fault">San Andreas Fault</a> known as the "Big Bend", where quake-recurrence tracking shows major activity roughly every 140–160 years. The closest portion of the San Andreas is actually 29 miles (47 km) from Glendale. The last major quake along the southern San Andreas was recorded in 1857.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1971_San_Fernando_earthquake" title="1971 San Fernando earthquake">1971 San Fernando earthquake</a>, which took place along the western edge of the Sierra Madre Fault, surface ruptures were nearly 12 miles (19 km) long, including one portion a few miles northwest of Glendale. Most of the damage was in the northern San Fernando Valley, though 31 structures in Glendale suffered major damage and had to be demolished, plus numerous chimneys collapsed. The <a href="/wiki/1994_Northridge_earthquake" title="1994 Northridge earthquake">1994 Northridge earthquake</a> had an epicenter about 18 miles (29 km) from Glendale. The city suffered severe damage to a public parking structure and sections of the <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Galleria" title="Glendale Galleria">Glendale Galleria</a> parking structures and exterior columns incurred damages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Glendale has a <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Csa</i>). The highest recorded temperature in Glendale was 110 °F (43 °C) on several occasions. The lowest recorded temperature was 17 °F (−8 °C) in February 2003. The warmest month is August and the coolest month is January. The rainfall is highest in February and lowest in July. The hills and mountains of northern Glendale very rarely have snow, owing to its warmer temperatures during the winter. It may only occur about every five to 10 years. The last time it snowed was February 26, 2011. Snow accumulations around 3 in were present; sleet was present, as well. Frost is common from late November to early March. Temperatures as low as 30 °F (−1 °C) do occur during the winter, but only once or twice. Heavy rains and thunderstorms are also common during the winter. The spring brings pleasant weather, with very little rain. The summer is usually fairly warm, with highs from 85 °F (29 °C), to the low 100s (40 °C). The highest temperature ever was 110 °F (43 °C). Summer can sometimes bring monsoon thunderstorms. Humidity can be very low, but it can also be very high, causing very steamy, muggy, and uncomfortable conditions. These days cause heat indices over 120 °F (49 °C). Fall brings nice weather, but can be gusty due to the Santa Ana winds, blowing in once or twice a year from October to December. Santa Ana winds can reach up to 70 miles per hour, with gusts up to 100 in mountain passes and canyons. One to eight thunderstorms occur in Glendale each year. Very rarely are they severe, but when they are, they are accompanied by gusty winds and hail.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">Parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The city has nearly 50 public parks, from Deukmejian Wilderness Park in the north to Cerritos Park in the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Central Park has the only West Coast monument to Korean <a href="/wiki/Comfort_women" title="Comfort women">comfort women</a> of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry_and_development">Industry and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Industry and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GlendaleCA_801NorthBrand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="667" data-file-width="500" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/GlendaleCA_801NorthBrand.jpg/220px-GlendaleCA_801NorthBrand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/GlendaleCA_801NorthBrand.jpg/330px-GlendaleCA_801NorthBrand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/GlendaleCA_801NorthBrand.jpg/440px-GlendaleCA_801NorthBrand.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GlendaleCA_801NorthBrand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
801 North Brand, one of Glendale's many modern skyscrapers: Companies such as <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=NexusLab&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="NexusLab (page does not exist)">NexusLab</a>, Great West Life, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Citi" title="Citi">Citi</a>, Unum, and <a href="/wiki/Cigna" title="Cigna">Cigna</a> have offices downtown.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Grand Central Airport was a municipal airport developed from 1923 which became the largest employer in Glendale for many years, and contributed to the development of aviation in the United States in many important ways. The main terminal building still stands and includes both Art Deco and Spanish-style architectural elements. The facility was the first official terminal for the Los Angeles area, as well as the departure point for the first commercial west-to-east transcontinental flight flown by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lindbergh" title="Charles Lindbergh">Charles Lindbergh</a>. During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the Grand Central Air Terminal building was camouflaged to protect it from enemy targeting. It was closed down in 1959, and made way for the Grand Central Business Centre, an <a href="/wiki/Industrial_park" title="Industrial park">industrial park</a>.</p>
<p>Forest Lawn Memorial Park started in Tropico (later annexed to Glendale) in 1906 and is famous for its art collection and the burial of many celebrities, as well as for the 1933 opening of the first funeral home on cemetery grounds anywhere in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bob%27s_Big_Boy" title="Bob's Big Boy">Bob's Big Boy</a> chain of <a href="/wiki/Hamburger" title="Hamburger">hamburger</a> restaurants started in Glendale on East Colorado in August 1936, and the <a href="/wiki/Baskin-Robbins" title="Baskin-Robbins">Baskin-Robbins</a> "31 Flavors" chain of <a href="/wiki/Ice_cream" title="Ice cream">ice cream</a> parlors started in Adams Square in 1945. The Glendale Public Library<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> on Harvard Street houses its "Special Collections" department which contains original documents and records on much of the history of Glendale. It also contains one of the largest collections of books on cats in the world, over 20,000 volumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-la_a_z-library_cats_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-la_a_z-library_cats-26">[26]</a></sup> It was donated to the library in the 1950s by the Jewel City Cat Fanciers Club, with the understanding that it would be made into a special collection and kept permanently for club members to use and enjoy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-personal_comm-library_cats_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-personal_comm-library_cats-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city experienced significant development in the 1970s, with the completion of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glendale_Freeway" title="Glendale Freeway">Glendale Freeway (Highway 2)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ventura_Freeway" title="Ventura Freeway">Ventura Freeway (Highway 134)</a>. This included redevelopment of Brand Boulevard, renovation of the 1925 <a href="/wiki/Alex_Theatre" title="Alex Theatre">Alex Theatre</a>, and construction of the <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Galleria" title="Glendale Galleria">Glendale Galleria</a> shopping mall which opened in 1976, and was further expanded in 1982.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NewCentral350.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="232" data-file-width="350" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/NewCentral350.jpg/220px-NewCentral350.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/NewCentral350.jpg/330px-NewCentral350.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c2/NewCentral350.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NewCentral350.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Public_Library" title="Glendale Public Library">Central Public Library</a> (1973)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Several large companies have offices in Glendale. The U.S. headquarters of the Swiss foods multinational <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IHOP_(restaurant)" title="IHOP (restaurant)">International House of Pancakes</a> are located in Glendale. The Los Angeles regional office of California's <a href="/wiki/State_Compensation_Insurance_Fund" title="State Compensation Insurance Fund">State Compensation Insurance Fund</a> is in Glendale. Americas United Bank was founded in Glendale in 2006 and is still headquartered there. <a href="/wiki/Nero_AG" title="Nero AG">Nero AG</a>, the software company that makes <a href="/wiki/Nero_Burning_ROM" title="Nero Burning ROM">Nero Burning ROM</a>, also has its main North American subsidiary located in Glendale. <a href="/wiki/Panda_Security" title="Panda Security">Panda Security</a>, a large antivirus software company, also has its principal U.S. office in Glendale. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neopets,_Inc." title="Neopets, Inc.">Neopets, Inc.</a>, a company that created the popular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virtual_pet" title="Virtual pet">virtual pet</a> website, <a href="/wiki/Neopets" title="Neopets">Neopets</a>, is located in the city (it was sold in 2005 to <a href="/wiki/Viacom" title="Viacom">Viacom</a>). In August 2013, <a href="/wiki/Avery_Dennison" title="Avery Dennison">Avery Dennison</a> Corp., a label maker for major brands, announced plans to move its headquarters from <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena</a> to Glendale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Avery employs about 26,000 people.</p>
<p>Glendale, along with Burbank, has served as a major production center for the U.S. entertainment industry and the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">animation</a> industry in particular for several decades, because <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">the Walt Disney Company</a> outgrew its Burbank studio lot in the early 1960s, and started expanding into the closest business park available, which happened to be Glendale's Grand Central Business Centre about two miles east. First came the headquarters for <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Imagineering" title="Walt Disney Imagineering">Imagineering</a>, followed in the 1980s by other divisions and offices. Today, Disney's Grand Central Creative Campus (known as GC3 for short) is home to <a href="/wiki/Disney_Consumer_Products" title="Disney Consumer Products">Consumer Products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Disney_Interactive" title="Disney Interactive">Disney Interactive</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Muppets_Studio" title="The Muppets Studio">the Muppets Studio</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marvel_Animation_Studios" title="Marvel Animation Studios">Marvel Animation Studios</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> From 1985 to 1995, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Animation_Studios" title="Walt Disney Animation Studios">Walt Disney Animation Studios</a> (then known as Walt Disney Feature Animation) was headquartered in the Grand Central Business Centre, meaning that most of the films of the <a href="/wiki/Disney_Renaissance" title="Disney Renaissance">Disney Renaissance</a> era were actually developed in Glendale. <a href="/wiki/DisneyToon_Studios" title="DisneyToon Studios">DisneyToon Studios</a>, a division of WDAS, is still located in the Grand Central Business Centre near GC3, along with the Animation Research Library, Disney Animation's archive. Disney-owned <a href="/wiki/KABC-TV" title="KABC-TV">KABC-TV</a> is located on Circle 7 Drive to the south of GC3.</p>
<p>In 1994, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Katzenberg" title="Jeffrey Katzenberg">Jeffrey Katzenberg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/David_Geffen" title="David Geffen">David Geffen</a> formed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DreamWorks_SKG" title="DreamWorks SKG">DreamWorks SKG</a>, a diversified entertainment company. <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Animation" title="DreamWorks Animation">DreamWorks Animation</a> remains located in the city's Grand Central Business Centre on land formerly occupied by a helicopter landing base next to the old airfield (and next to KABC-TV). Thus, many American animators who worked on feature films in the 1990s and 2000s have spent large portions of their careers in Glendale working for Disney or DreamWorks.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Americana_at_Brand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="1536" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/The_Americana_at_Brand.jpg/220px-The_Americana_at_Brand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/The_Americana_at_Brand.jpg/330px-The_Americana_at_Brand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/The_Americana_at_Brand.jpg/440px-The_Americana_at_Brand.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Americana_at_Brand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Americana_at_Brand" title="Americana at Brand">Americana at Brand</a> (2008)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2005, construction began near the Galleria of developer <a href="/wiki/Caruso_Affiliated" title="Caruso Affiliated">Rick Caruso</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Americana_at_Brand" title="Americana at Brand">Americana at Brand</a>", a 15.5-acre (63,000 m<sup>2</sup>) outdoor shopping and residential community. Caruso had previously designed and built <a href="/wiki/The_Grove_at_Farmers_Market" title="The Grove at Farmers Market">the Grove at Farmers Market</a>. The new Glendale development was opened to the public on May 2, 2008, and features 75 shops and restaurants, 238 apartments, 100 condominiums, and a <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Theatres" title="Pacific Theatres">Pacific Theatres</a> 18-plex Cinema which seats 3000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2011 study by an outside consulting organization hired by the city showed that people felt Glendale was boring, though many beloved animated films have been created by Disney and DreamWorks in Glendale. After seeing the results of the study, the Glendale City Council voted to appropriate $1 million to undertake an image campaign based on the tagline: "Your Life. Animated." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Shopping">Shopping</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Shopping">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Glendale has a wide selection for shoppers, one being the <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Galleria" title="Glendale Galleria">Glendale Galleria</a>, which is anchored by <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy's">Macy's</a>, <a href="/wiki/Target_Corporation" title="Target Corporation">Target</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._C._Penney" title="J. C. Penney">J. C. Penney</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bloomingdales" title="Bloomingdales">Bloomingdales</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Americana_at_Brand" title="Americana at Brand">Americana at Brand</a>, which is an upscale outdoor mall (similar to <a href="/wiki/The_Grove_at_Farmers_Market" title="The Grove at Farmers Market">the Grove at Farmers Market</a> in L.A.) which includes stores such as <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co." title="Tiffany &amp; Co.">Tiffany &amp; Co.</a>, <a href="/wiki/H%26M" title="H&amp;M">H&amp;M</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armani_Exchange" title="Armani Exchange">Armani Exchange</a>, <a href="/wiki/True_Religion_(clothing_brand)" title="True Religion (clothing brand)">True Religion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forever_21" title="Forever 21">Forever 21</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Urban_Outfitters" title="Urban Outfitters">Urban Outfitters</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> The Americana at Brand is home to a <a href="/wiki/Nordstrom" title="Nordstrom">Nordstrom</a>, which was previously located inside the Glendale Galleria. Another shopping area is the Glendale Fashion Center, which is anchored by <a href="/wiki/Ross" title="Ross">Ross</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TJ_Maxx" title="TJ Maxx">TJ Maxx</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nordstrom_Rack" title="Nordstrom Rack">Nordstrom Rack</a>, <a href="/wiki/Staples_Inc." title="Staples Inc.">Staples</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Petco" title="Petco">Petco</a>. Shopping can also be done at Montrose Shopping Park in North Glendale. The shopping park runs down Honolulu Avenue and is filled with many stores and restaurants.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" title="2010 United States Census">2010 United States Census</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> reported that Glendale had a population of 191,719. The <a href="/wiki/Population_density" title="Population density">population density</a> was 6,268.6 people per square mile (2,420.3/km²). The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(United_States_Census)" title="Race (United States Census)">racial makeup</a> of Glendale was 136,226 (71.1%) White, 2,573 (1.3%) Black, 531 (0.3%) Native American, 31,434 (16.4%) Asian (6.9% Filipino, 5.4% Korean, 1.3% Chinese), 122 (0.1%) Pacific Islander, 12,146 (6.3%) from other races, and 8,687 (4.5%) from two or more races. Hispanics or Latinos of any race were 33,414 persons (17.4%). Non-Hispanic Whites were 61.5% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quif_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-quif-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The census reported that 190,290 people (99.3% of the population) lived in households, 223 (0.1%) lived in noninstitutionalized group quarters, and 1,206 (0.6%) were institutionalized. Of the 72,269 households, 21,792 (30.2%) had children under the age of 18 living in them, 37,486 (51.9%) were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">opposite-sex married couples</a> living together, 8,908 (12.3%) had a female householder with no husband present, 3,693 (5.1%) had a male householder with no wife present, 2,359 (3.3%) were <a href="/wiki/POSSLQ" title="POSSLQ">unmarried opposite-sex partnerships</a>, and 605 (0.8%) were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Same-sex_partnerships" title="Same-sex partnerships">same-sex married couples or partnerships</a>. About 18,000 households (24.9%) were made up of individuals, and 7,077 (9.8%) had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.63. The 50,087 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Family_(U.S._Census)" title="Family (U.S. Census)">families</a> (69.3% of all households) had an average family size of 3.19.</p>
<p>In the city, the population was distributed as 35,732 (18.6%) under the age of 18, 16,609 (8.7%) aged 18 to 24, 54,518 (28.4%) aged 25 to 44, 54,942 (28.7%) aged 45 to 64, and 29,918 (15.6%) who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 41.0 years. For every 100 females, there were 91.1 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 87.9 males.</p>
<p>The 76,269 housing units averaged 2,493.8 per square mile (962.8/km²), of which 27,535 (38.1%) were owner-occupied, and 44,734 (61.9%) were occupied by renters. The homeowner vacancy rate was 1.3%; the rental vacancy rate was 5.5%; 76,769 people (40.0% of the population) lived in owner-occupied housing units and 113,521 people (59.2%) lived in rental housing units.</p>
<p>During 2009–2013, Glendale had a median household income of $53,020, with 14.2% of the population living below the federal poverty line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quif_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-quif-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000">2000</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2000">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As of the <a href="/wiki/Census" title="Census">census</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GR2_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-GR2-36">[36]</a></sup> of 2000, there were 194,973 people, 71,805 households, and 49,617 families residing in the city. The population density was 6,362.2 inhabitants per square mile (2,456.1/km²). There were 73,713 housing units averaged 2,405.3 per square mile (928.6/km²). The racial makeup of the city was 63.6% White, 1.6% Black, 0.3% Native American, 16.1% Asian American, 0.1% Pacific Islander, 8.6% from other races, and 10.1% from two or more races. About 19.7% of the population was Hispanic or Latino of any race.</p>
<p>Of the 71,805 households, 32.9% had children under the age of 18 living with them, 52.3% were <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">married couples</a> living together, 11.8% had a female householder with no husband present, and 30.9% were not families; 25.7% of all households were made up of individuals and 8.7% had someone living alone who was 65 years of age or older. The average household size was 2.68 and the average family size was 3.27.</p>
<p>In the city, the population was distributed as 22.4% under the age of 18, 8.4% from 18 to 24, 32.2% from 25 to 44, 23.1% from 45 to 64, and 13.9% who were 65 years of age or older. The median age was 38 years. For every 100 females, there were 91.3 males. For every 100 females age 18 and over, there were 88.0 males.</p>
<p>The median income for a household in the city was $41,805, and for a family was $47,633. Males had a median income of $39,709 versus $33,815 for females. The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> for the city was $22,227. About 13.6% of families and 15.5% of the population were below the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty_line" title="Poverty line">poverty line</a>, including 20.7% of those under age 18 and 11.9% of those age 65 or over.</p>
<p>In June 2000, Erin Texeira of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> stated that according to data from the US Census and the City of Glendale, the populations were about 30% Armenians, 25% other White, 25% Latino and Hispanic, and 16% Asian.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Texeirap1_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Texeirap1-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armenian_population">Armenian population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Armenian population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Armenian_Americans_in_Los_Angeles" title="History of the Armenian Americans in Los Angeles">History of the Armenian Americans in Los Angeles</a></div>
<p>Armenian families have lived in the city since the 1920s, but the surge in immigration escalated in the 1970s. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian_American" title="Armenian American">Armenian Americans</a> are well integrated into the city, with many businesses, several Armenian schools, and ethnic/cultural organizations serving this ethnic group. Most of the Armenians in Glendale arrived in the city in the past two decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The city of Glendale is home to one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Largest_Armenian_communities_outside_of_Armenia" title="Largest Armenian communities outside of Armenia">largest Armenian communities outside of Armenia</a>.</p>
<p>Beginning in the late 1980s, with assistance from family and friends already there, Armenians from the former Soviet Union began arriving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Texeirap1_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-Texeirap1-17">[17]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Unified_School_District" title="Glendale Unified School District">Glendale Unified School District</a>, by 1988, along with students from the Middle East, they had become the largest ethnic group in the public schools, now having a larger number than the Latinos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CliffordRoark2_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-CliffordRoark2-38">[38]</a></sup> Glendale became the municipality with the largest number of ethnic Armenians other than <a href="/wiki/Yerevan" title="Yerevan">Yerevan</a>. Rick Young, a Glendale Police Department spokesperson, stated, "In five to eight years, the [Armenian] community went from a few thousand to about 40,000."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Texeirap1_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-Texeirap1-17">[17]</a></sup> Levon Marashlian, an instructor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian_history" title="Armenian history">Armenian history</a> at <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Community_College_(California)" title="Glendale Community College (California)">Glendale College</a>, stated that in the early 1990s Glendale's Armenian community became the largest in the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_metropolitan_area" title="Los Angeles metropolitan area">Los Angeles metropolitan area</a>, surpassing the Armenian community of Hollywood.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Texeirap1_17-4"><a href="#cite_note-Texeirap1-17">[17]</a></sup> Alice Petrossian, the GUSD director of intercultural education, stated that Burbank lies within the middle of other Armenian communities, so it attracted Armenians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CliffordRoark2_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-CliffordRoark2-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>A new headquarters of the Armenian National Committee/Western Region opened in 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> By 1999, about 25% of the population spoke Armenian and there were many Armenian businesses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> By 2005 the Armenian population was 40% of the total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CovarrubiasArme_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-CovarrubiasArme-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_2000_Census" title="United States 2000 Census">United States 2000 Census</a>, Glendale is home to 65,343 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian-American" title="Armenian-American">Armenian-Americans</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> (making up 34.1% of the total population), increasing from 1990 when there were 31,402 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Armenian-American" title="Armenian-American">Armenian-Americans</a> in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> As of 2005, one-third of Los Angeles' estimated 153,000 Armenians, or 51,000 around a quarter of Glendale's 205,000 residents was Armenian. At that time, Armenians held a majority on the Glendale city council,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> and it had done so since that year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CovarrubiasArme_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-CovarrubiasArme-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2005 Armenian businesses include bakeries, coffee shops, and restaurants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CovarrubiasArme_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-CovarrubiasArme-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of November 2015, three of the five members of Glendale's city council are of Armenian descent: Mayor <a href="/wiki/Ara_Najarian" title="Ara Najarian">Ara Najarian</a> and councilmembers <a href="/wiki/Zareh_Sinanyan" title="Zareh Sinanyan">Zareh Sinanyan</a> (mayor from April 2014 to April 2015) and Vartan Gharpetian. Former Armenian-American mayors of Glendale include <a href="/wiki/Larry_Zarian" title="Larry Zarian">Larry Zarian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Yousefian" title="Bob Yousefian">Bob Yousefian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rafi_Manoukian" title="Rafi Manoukian">Rafi Manoukian</a>.</p>
<p>Some outspoken members of the highly successful Armenian-American rock band, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/System_Of_A_Down" title="System Of A Down">System Of A Down</a>, were based in Glendale at the time of formation. These include singer <a href="/wiki/Serj_Tankian" title="Serj Tankian">Serj Tankian</a> and bassist <a href="/wiki/Shavo_Odadjian" title="Shavo Odadjian">Shavo Odadjian</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ethnic_groups">Other ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Other ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Mexican American community was established in Glendale by the 1960s. The late 1980s and the early 1990s also saw increases in Mexican American population as Glendale offers a safer suburban environment away from the city with higher quality education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Texeirap1_17-5"><a href="#cite_note-Texeirap1-17">[17]</a></sup> After the Persian Revolution, many Persians migrated into the cities seeking a suburban city with lower crime and quality education.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LAT_1990-02-13_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-LAT_1990-02-13-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_government">Local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Peterson_Historic_House_and_its_restored_pergola.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/The_Peterson_Historic_House_and_its_restored_pergola.jpg/220px-The_Peterson_Historic_House_and_its_restored_pergola.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/The_Peterson_Historic_House_and_its_restored_pergola.jpg/330px-The_Peterson_Historic_House_and_its_restored_pergola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/The_Peterson_Historic_House_and_its_restored_pergola.jpg/440px-The_Peterson_Historic_House_and_its_restored_pergola.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Peterson_Historic_House_and_its_restored_pergola.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Peterson House is on the local historic register.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the city's most recent comprehensive annual financial report, the city's various funds had $575.6 million in revenues, $542.8 million in expenditures, $2,089.7 million in total assets, $480.9 million in total liabilities, and $460.4 million in cash and investments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-City_of_Glendale_CAFR_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-City_of_Glendale_CAFR-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="County_representation">County representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: County representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County_Department_of_Health_Services" title="Los Angeles County Department of Health Services">Los Angeles County Department of Health Services</a> operates the Glendale Health Center in Glendale.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_and_federal_representation">State and federal representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: State and federal representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>, Glendale is in <a href="/wiki/California%27s_28th_congressional_district" title="California's 28th congressional district">California's 28th congressional district</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Adam_Schiff" title="Adam Schiff">Adam Schiff</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/California_State_Legislature" title="California State Legislature">California State Legislature</a>, Glendale is in <a href="/wiki/California%27s_25th_State_Senate_district" title="California's 25th State Senate district">the 25th Senate District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Portantino" title="Anthony Portantino">Anthony Portantino</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/California%27s_43rd_State_Assembly_district" title="California's 43rd State Assembly district">the 43rd Assembly District</a>, represented by <a href="/wiki/California_Democratic_Party" title="California Democratic Party">Democrat</a> <a href="/wiki/Laura_Friedman" title="Laura Friedman">Laura Friedman</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swd_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-swd-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement_and_services">Law enforcement and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Law enforcement and services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Glendale,_California" title="Crime in Glendale, California">Crime in Glendale, California</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glendale_Fire_Department_truck_in_Burbank_2015-01-19.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1714" data-file-width="2400" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Glendale_Fire_Department_truck_in_Burbank_2015-01-19.jpg/220px-Glendale_Fire_Department_truck_in_Burbank_2015-01-19.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Glendale_Fire_Department_truck_in_Burbank_2015-01-19.jpg/330px-Glendale_Fire_Department_truck_in_Burbank_2015-01-19.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Glendale_Fire_Department_truck_in_Burbank_2015-01-19.jpg/440px-Glendale_Fire_Department_truck_in_Burbank_2015-01-19.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glendale_Fire_Department_truck_in_Burbank_2015-01-19.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
GFD engine 27</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Glendale maintains its own police department, which operates from its main station in downtown Glendale, its downtown substation in the <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Galleria" title="Glendale Galleria">Glendale Galleria</a>, and the Montrose substation in Verdugo City. The <a href="/wiki/California_Highway_Patrol" title="California Highway Patrol">California Highway Patrol</a> has its Southern Division Headquarters on Central Avenue in downtown Glendale.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fire_department">Fire department</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Fire department">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Fire protection is provided by the Glendale Fire Department (GFD). The GFD is an all-risk, career fire protection agency, responding to about 17,000 emergency and nonemergency calls for service annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The GFD consists of nine strategically located fire stations, with mutual aid provided by the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_County_Fire_Department" title="Los Angeles County Fire Department">Los Angeles County Fire Department</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_City_Fire_Department" title="Los Angeles City Fire Department">Los Angeles City Fire Department</a>, Burbank Fire Department, and Pasadena Fire Department. The department maintains a "Class 1" ISO rating as part of certification through the Public Protection Classification program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Verdugo_Fire_Communications_Center">Verdugo Fire Communications Center</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Verdugo Fire Communications Center">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Verdugo FCC was established on August 1, 1979, between the cities of <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank</a>, Glendale, and <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_California" title="Pasadena, California">Pasadena</a> as a way to consolidate fire dispatching and telecommunications between the departments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Presently, Verdugo provides services to all 13 fire departments in the California OES "Area C" mutual aid plan, making them a regional dispatch center.</p>
<p>The center is stationed on the third floor of Glendale Fire Department's headquarters (Fire Station 21) and handles roughly 72,000 calls for service annually.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The fire chiefs from Burbank, Glendale and Pasadena oversee the center under a <a href="/wiki/Joint_powers_authority" title="Joint powers authority">joint powers authority</a>. These cities contract services from the center: <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hope_Airport" title="Bob Hope Airport">Bob Hope Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Pasadena,_California" title="South Pasadena, California">South Pasadena</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Marino,_California" title="San Marino, California">San Marino</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Gabriel,_California" title="San Gabriel, California">San Gabriel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arcadia,_California" title="Arcadia, California">Arcadia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Monrovia,_California" title="Monrovia, California">Monrovia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre,_California" title="Sierra Madre, California">Sierra Madre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montebello,_California" title="Montebello, California">Montebello</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alhambra,_California" title="Alhambra, California">Alhambra</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Monterey_Park,_California" title="Monterey Park, California">Monterey Park</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_safety_statistics">Public safety statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Public safety statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, Glendale was named the ninth-safest city in America in a report published by 24/7 Wall Street based on violent crime rates in cities with more than 100,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> Also in 2014, real estate company Movoto used FBI data crime data from 2013 to conduct a study of 100 U.S. cities with populations between 126,047 and 210,309 residents and concluded that Glendale was the safest mid-sized city in America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Unified_School_District" title="Glendale Unified School District">Glendale Unified School District</a> operates the public schools in Glendale. The GUSD high schools include <a href="/wiki/Glendale_High_School_(Glendale,_California)" title="Glendale High School (Glendale, California)">Glendale High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Hoover_High_School_(Glendale)" title="Herbert Hoover High School (Glendale)">Herbert Hoover High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clark_Magnet_High_School" title="Clark Magnet High School">Clark Magnet High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crescenta_Valley_High_School" title="Crescenta Valley High School">Crescenta Valley High School</a> located in La Crescenta and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Allan_F._Daily_High_School&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Allan F. Daily High School (page does not exist)">Allan F. Daily High School</a>. A number of private schools also operate in Glendale, including Chamlian Armenian School,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Holy_Family_High_School_(Glendale,_California)" title="Holy Family High School (Glendale, California)">Holy Family High School</a>, Salem Lutheran School, and Glendale Adventist Academy. Glendale is also home to <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Community_College_(California)" title="Glendale Community College (California)">Glendale Community College</a>. Middle schools are Roosevelt Middle School, Toll Middle School, Rosemont Middle School, and Wilson Middle School.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Glendale community news is covered by the <i><a href="/wiki/Glendale_News-Press" title="Glendale News-Press">Glendale News-Press</a></i>, which was founded in 1905.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glendale_Station" title="Glendale Station">Glendale Station</a></div>
<p>Glendale offers many transportation options. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/LADOT" title="LADOT">LADOT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metro_Local" title="Metro Local">Metro Local</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metro_Rapid" title="Metro Rapid">Metro Rapid</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Glendale_Beeline" title="Glendale Beeline">Glendale Beeline</a> all have buses that run in the city. Glendale Transportation Center provides connections to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greyhound_bus" title="Greyhound bus">Greyhound buses</a> and three train lines. Glendale is also served by four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freeway" title="Freeway">freeways</a>: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glendale_Freeway" title="Glendale Freeway">Glendale Freeway</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Route_2" title="State Route 2">State Route 2</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Ventura_Freeway" title="Ventura Freeway">Ventura Freeway</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ventura_Freeway#State_Route_134" title="Ventura Freeway">State Route 134</a>), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foothill_Freeway" title="Foothill Freeway">Foothill Freeway</a> (<a href="/wiki/Interstate_210_and_State_Route_210_(California)" title="Interstate 210 and State Route 210 (California)">Interstate 210</a>) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_State_Freeway" title="Golden State Freeway">Golden State Freeway</a> (<a href="/wiki/Interstate_5" title="Interstate 5">Interstate 5</a>).</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities">Sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Glendale,_California&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Glendale has six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sister_cities" title="Sister cities">sister cities</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>

<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico"><img alt="Mexico" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="840" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/35px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/46px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <b><a href="/wiki/Tlaquepaque" title="Tlaquepaque">Tlaquepaque</a></b>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico"><img alt="Mexico" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="840" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/23px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/35px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Flag_of_Mexico.svg/46px-Flag_of_Mexico.svg.png 2x" width="23"/></a></span> <b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rosarito" title="Rosarito">Rosarito</a></b>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a></li>
